The author of this book, having completed for you, my sons, this book which is a part of the knowledge in medicine with its completeness and where the aim has been reached from its clarity and elucidation, saw fit to complete it for you through this article which is a part of the work by hand.
For the work by hand is improved in our country and in our time, it is entirely absent; so much so that its study was almost abandoned and its effect faded. Only a few minor notes remained in the original books, which have been distorted by hands, and faced with errors and obfuscation; thus, their meanings were lost and their benefits were obscured.
I saw it fit to revive and write this article about it on the path of explanation, elucidation, and concision, providing illustrations for each instrument and all tools of work; as these are an increase in clarification and an essential resource.
The reason being that there is no craftsman skilled in his hand in our time, due to the length of medical craftsmanship which requires him to be well-versed in anatomy as described by Galen before embarking on it. So that one can understand the benefits of organs, their structure, sensitivity and interaction, as well as knowledge about bones, nerves, muscles and their numbers, exits and arteries, veins, sinuses and their exits, places of their exits.
Therefore, the novices say that doctors by name are many but in reality few, especially among handcraftsmen; we have mentioned this on one side at the beginning of this book.
For whoever is not knowledgeable about what we mentioned regarding anatomy, it would inevitably lead them to make a mistake that could kill people as I have witnessed with many who portrayed this knowledge without understanding or expertise.
And thus, I have seen an unlearned surgeon cut into a piggy tumor in the neck of a woman, severing some vessels of the neck until she bled to death right before his eyes.
And I have seen another surgeon who advanced in the removal of a stone from a man who had pricked his kidney; the stone was large and caused much commotion, but he removed it with a piece of bladder. The man died around three days later, and I was called upon to remove it. From the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, I could assess what I would face.
And I have seen another doctor who was supported by some of our local military leaders in the field of medicine.
And it happened to a black slave who had a break near the ankle with an injury. The doctor rushed without hesitation, gripping the fracture tightly against the wound with ligatures and splints in a manner that cut off all possibility of breathing for the injury.
Then he indulged him in his desires, then left him for days and ordered that no bandage be removed until his leg and foot swelled up, watching over his demise.
And I called him, rushing to remove the bandage; he found relief and alleviation from his pains. However, decomposition had set in deeply within the limb, and I was unable to dislodge it.
And decay continued to ravage the limb until death ensued.
And I have seen another surgeon who treated a black cancer, it would blister after days until it became large for the patient. It was this: if cancer is of a pure mixed black essence, then it should not be exposed to iron completely.
Unless it is in regard to a limb where one may consider amputation.
For this reason, my children, you should learn that work with your hands divides into two: one accompanied by safety and the other often met with difficulty in most cases.
And warnings have been given in every place where danger and fear are involved, it is necessary for you to be aware of these and avoid them.
So that the ignorant do not find the path to speech and criticism, take firmness and prudence for yourselves, and treat your illnesses with kindness and perseverance.
And use the best path leading to safety and commendable outcome, and be prepared for dangerous illnesses that are difficult to cure.
And purify yourselves from whatever you fear might lead to suspicion in your religion and worldly affairs, for it is better for you both here and in the afterlife according to your fate.
And Galen, in some of his instructions, said: Do not treat illness with evil; call yourselves doctors of evil instead.

The first door.
In the knee.
And before we discuss its use, it is necessary to mention the way of its benefits and drawbacks and in what mood it is used.
And I say that speaking about the manner of benefitting from the knee and its drawbacks is a long and precise knowledge, a secret hidden truth, and many wise people have spoken on this topic.
And they differed in their views about it. I have abbreviated my brief discussion to avoid lengthening the explanation.
And I say that the knee benefits in general for all bad moods, whether with a substance or without one. There are two types of mood: the hot mood without substance and the dry mood without substance.
As for the dry mood with substance, they differ in it. Some say that using the knee is beneficial there while others oppose this view, stating that fire, which causes heat and dryness, does not suit a disease of this nature.
It is impossible to be cured of a hot, dry illness with a treatment that itself is hot and dry. The one who argues against this states that the knee treated with fire can be beneficial for a hot, dry disease that occurs in people's bodies. Because if you add the body and its moisture to the fire mood, you will make the human body cold.
And I say as he says because the experience has shown me that to this matter it should not be imagined without experiencing and going through the process of understanding deeply in the topic of the knee. This is about stopping on the differences in moods of people and conditions within themselves, causes of their illnesses, symptoms, and duration of time for each one.
And as for other moods, there is no fear from them for you and especially cold wet illnesses; all the physicians agree on it and they do not differ in benefiting from it.
Know this, my sons, that healing through fire and its advantage over treatment with burning medicine lies in the fact that fire is a unique substance whose effect is limited to the organ it penetrates and does not harm another connected organ except for minimal damage.
And healing with burning medicine might extend its effect beyond the organ and perhaps cause a difficult to cure disease in it, or maybe kill. And because of its honor and magnificence is nature of fire; that's what she does unless she went overboard.
And we have clarified that through experience by extending our service and care for the profession, and standing firm on the truth of the matter.
For this reason, I refrained from lengthy speech, even though it would not be fitting for my book, I have discussed with you in secret the mystery of fire and how it works in bodies, and refuted its effects on diseases using philosophical, proof-based language to clarify your understanding.
Know this, my sons, that they have differed about the time in which fire is to be used and made of spring time the best period for it.
And I say that fire may be used at any time, because the harm caused by time can be absorbed in the benefit brought about by the use of fire. And especially if the fire is from necessary strong pains that cannot bear delay, for fear of what might follow it which could be worse than the harm caused by time itself.
Do not let yourselves be deceived, my sons, by the common misconceptions and the folly of many doctors. Know that there is no return for a disease which a cure has been found for, do not blame it.
And do not assume that the cure is only like a medicine that changes mood and dries up moisture, which is the cause of pains.
However, the cure prefers over medicine in terms of the speed of its success, strength of its action and intensity of its power.
But the disease might return at some point in time depending on the mood of the patient and the success, strength, and intensity of the illness, as well as what accumulates in his body from excesses and neglecting himself in acquiring food and so forth among its causes.
God, let the disease that the cure is used for be a mild one and in an organ with little excesses and moisture. Like the cure for pain, for example, and similar conditions; it might be that this pain does not recur. This would at least be the case.
And as for the common belief that the cure is the end of medicine, it's a correct statement but not according to what others say because they believe there's no cure that benefits with medicine or without after the occurrence of the cure. The situation is different from this.
And the meaning of 'the cure is the end of medicine' only means that when we have tried various treatments for a disease, and those medicines did not work, then we resort to the last thing which is the cure, and if it works from this point onwards, then indeed the cure is the end of medicine. There is no meaning in what the general public and many of the doctors misunderstand.
And I mentioned at the beginning that gold plating is better than iron plating, and they said so because of the balance in the quality of gold and its excellence. They also claimed that it doesn't corrode the place where the plating is done, which is not true at all.
And I have tried this myself and found that it only works on some bodies not others. Gold plating is better than iron as they said, but the problem arises when you protect the hearth in fire from gold; you won't be able to determine when it heats up to the desired temperature for the redness of the gold.
And because it speeds up the cooling process; if you increase its heat in fever, it melts in fire. Due to this, craftsmen become confused with this matter and thus gold plating is faster and more accurate for work if God wills.

The first section.
In the gold plating of the head, there is one method.
This method of gold plating is useful against the dampness and cold that affect the brain, both causes of headaches, as well as frequent head colds extending to the eyes and ears, frequent sleepiness, toothaches, and sore throats. In short, for every illness that appears due to cold, such as fevers, convulsions, fainting, and so on.
The picture of this method is that you should first instruct the patient to take a purgative medicine for the relief of head congestion for three or four nights, depending on what is prescribed according to the strength of the patient, their age, and habits.
Then command him to shave his head like Moses, then place him before you sitting with his hands on his chest.
Then place the tip of your hand on the tip of his nose between his eyes. Wherever your middle finger ends, teach that location using a stylus.
Then heat the oil lamp which is shown here.
Expose as much of the bone as would be equal to the diameter of a human skull or a pear, then raise your hand and if it cools down replace it with the same hammer or another one if it gets cold. Until you see the part of the bone as I have described to you. Then take a bit of salt and dissolve it in water, soak a piece of cotton in it, place it on the spot, and leave it for three days.
Then apply a piece of cotton that has been soaked in animal fat to him, leaving it on until the irritation from the heat disappears. Then treat him with the fourfold ointment until he recovers, if God willing.
They said that the wound becomes better and more effective as it remains open, discharging pus.
Some of them advised that the skin should be heated to the bone and that the iron should be held until some of the bone becomes burned, then after that remove what has been burned from the bone and treat.
Others said that it should be heated excessively until its effect is strong enough to cause the bone to break down, resulting in fragments as small as a carob or a small walnut. They claimed that vapor from this area rises and allows the wound to remain open for a long time.
Then it is treated until it disappears, and I do not consider these types of pus fundamentally except in some people. On the way of risk, leaving it with me is better. If it occurs, the head doubles whenever its natural connection separates, as we have seen in all other members.
And especially if the head of pus is naturally weak. The first type of pus has converted and it's better for me, I'll use it if God willing, and apply it accordingly.

The Third Chapter.
In the case of the temporary sister.
If a headache occurs in the forehead accompanied by a migraine, and the pain extends to the eye, you should expel the body fluids using medications that purify the head, and use all other treatments mentioned for disease categories. If this does not work, there are two possibilities for her. Either by using the burning acute medicine or by using iron.
If treatment by burning medicine, then take a single clove of garlic, peel it and cut its ends from both sides. Then make an incision in the place of pain with a broad dental tool until there is a spot under the skin that can accommodate the clove.
Then it should enter under the skin until it disappears, then pull on it with tight pulls and leave it for about fifteen hours. Then remove it and take out the garlic and leave the wound for two or three days before carrying on.
Cover the area with a cotton ball soaked in oil until pus starts to come out, then treat it with ointment until it heals if Allah wills. If you wish, do this with some of the burning medicines I mentioned in the eighteenth article about burning medicines.
And if treatment by iron is to be done, it will be like this: heat the iron which has this shape:.
The iron rod is called the pierce due to its shape where it has some curvature at its head, and in the middle of it there's a small notch.
Then place it on the painful area and hold your hand while you spin the iron slightly, very slightly. The amount of heat that burns the skin should be like half of its thickness. Raise your hand to prevent the burning of the artery below which causes bleeding, then dip a cotton into salt water and place it on the spot, leaving it for three days. Then apply the cotton with some fat, then treat it with a lotion until it heals if God wills.
And if you wish, sharpen this needle from the hammer and take care not to cut the artery in this temporary lesion specially.

The sixteenth chapter.
In the corner of the eye lid.
If its eyelashes turn inward and scratch the inside of the eye, there are two types in the corner [of the eyelid]. It is either by fire or by burning medicine, and if it is by fire then you order the afflicted one to abstain from touching his eyelashes until they grow out and become even.
If his eyelashes stick when they grow back, you tie his eyes with a band to prevent them from moving until they grow out and become even. When they do grow out and are even, place the head of the afflicted person on a stone and then draw a mark on the eyelid in the shape of an asafoetida leaf using a reed.
The mark begins near the eyelashes, then under the lower lid you place cotton soaked in egg white or saliva of the camel snout. Then heat your iron until it resembles this shape.
Then you apply the heated shape to the skin little by little in many repetitions until the surface of the skin resembling an asafoetida leaf is completely burned off. A sign that your operation was successful is when you see the eyelid turn white and the hair has risen from the eye lid.
Then raise your hand and leave him for three days. Afterwards, apply cotton dipped in oil until the scab comes off, then treat him with medicine until he recovers if God wills. If any hair returns after a while and relaxes the eyelid, this is an indication of healing.
Repeat the treatment in that area as you did at first. If hair is found on the lower eyelid, pull it out until it returns to its natural position and does not fall into the eye. As for treatment with burning medicine, you should order the afflicted one to refrain from touching his eyelashes until they grow out evenly.
Then create from the paper a sheet of skin, then take ordinary soap and unlit tallow from each, weighing about dirham or similar, grind them thoroughly into a good grind, and do this with the wheel so that they don't dry out. Then spread it onto the paper which you have made into the shape of an ace sheet, and place it on one or both eyelids. Place under the eye cotton soaked in egg white, and place the tip of the garlic inside your hand.
Place your index finger over the medicine and gently compress it. As you move it, touch the garlic to the medicine when you feel a sensation of heat from the garlic because it finds pleasure similar to fire in it. If it keeps finding the heat, leave the medicine alone and move it with your finger. When the heat ceases, remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And observe, if you see that the eyelid has risen as it rises when burned with fire or cuttings and if not, apply more medicine to the spot where the medicine did not work and was not cured until you complete your task and burn the eye. Then place cotton with fat on it until the scab of the burn falls off.
Then, treat it with the donkey's milk ointment or another until it heals. It is advisable for you when working to be extremely cautious that nothing falls into the eye from the medicine; if the eyelid relaxes after days and there's a bit of hair in the eye, we fear it might cause damage.
Then, apply the medicine to the spot that relaxed in the eyelid specifically as you did at first, then treat it until it heals. This is a sheet of paper resembling an ace.
Know that people's eyes may vary in size, so according to this, let your treatment be for them as well, it is not a secret path of rightness for those who have expertise in such matters.

In it, the contractions and the relaxed condition of the larynx.

The twenty-first chapter.
In it, the pain of the larynx.
If the larynx pain is due to cold or there are maggots inside and if the treatment with medicines does not relieve it, there are two ways to treat in this case, either by buttering (applying butter) or by burning (applying heat).
If it is regarding tallow, then take cow's tallow and boil it in an iron pot or a pot made of copper. Then take some cotton and twist it on the tip of a medical tool, dip it into the boiled tallow and place it onto the painful tooth using the wheel motion, hold it until it cools down.
Then repeat this several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth. Alternatively, you may dip wool or cotton into cold tallow and place it onto the painful tooth, then put a protected nail over it so that the fire can reach to the bottom of the tooth.
And if it's done with fire, you should use a copper or iron tube, there must be some water in its body so that the heat of the fire doesn't reach inside the tooth. Then heat up the iron rod until it reaches the shape, place it on the same tooth and hold your hand until the rod cools down. Do this several times.
If the pain goes away either that same day or another, then after this treatment, the patient should fill their mouth with good tallow and hold it for an hour, then throw it out. This is what the iron rod looks like.
You can heat it on any side and according to what is possible, this is how the tube appears.

Then, from every side, she should be applied until the entire decay is excised without leaving any residue at all. Then leave it for three days and apply powdered sulfur with oil to the areas heated by the charcoal iron, so that all the skin scales are removed along with all of the decay.
Then treat it with herbal ointments for the meat, and if after three days I see that the meat has grown healthily without any decay, otherwise reapply the fire to what remains of the decaying parts. The ulcer can be treated with strong medicine as well.
He serves the function of fire more effectively and efficiently. I mentioned treating it with strong medicine in Part Three; take it from there whenever you need it.
The Third and Fifty-First Chapter.
In using inverted and non-inverted needles.
Often, this reason occurs in the heels of the feet. It is a hard thing that grabs the heel and there are two aspects to it: either heating it with fire or soaking it in sharp water.
As for heating it with fire, this involves heating a dried heated iron brush resembling an eagle's feather made of iron around the entire circumference of the nail and making it thin at the edge. Then apply it on the nail, then move your hand with the iron brush around the nail until the iron brush reaches to the depth of the nail.
She leaves it for three days to benefit from the pus, then applies it with a heated and salted broom on the plaster, leaving the dressing overnight; it comes off from its roots. Then she treats the wound site with herbal ointment for scabies until it heals, if the nails are not bent back.
This often occurs on the surface of the body, particularly in hands and feet. It's recommended to use a brass tube or iron pipe or an eagle's feather brush, dipping it into a small amount of sharp water, then lowering it onto the nail or splinter.
Hold your hand as you move it slightly in a small flick motion, allowing the edge of the tube to affect the root of the nail. The sharp water will find its way into the root of the nail and allow the patient to endure for a short time on the sting of the sharp water.
Then leave it; the nail will come off completely. Do this to each one until you have treated all parts of the body that are affected, then treat their sites after they heal with ointments that promote flesh growth.
The forty-fifth chapter.
In discussing the nail.
If frostbite affects a nail, or fever to one quarter of the body or otherwise, four or five needles should be inserted between each spinal needle in his back and one needle in his chest. And on his stomach, a needle is placed with the oil-dipping method; then frostbite settles and the progress of the cold disease accelerates.
The fifty-fifth chapter.
In discussing the sudden bladder affliction in the body.
Sometimes, in the body pus may erupt which consists of thick foul matter from cold, rotten materials. Upon its first appearance, one should prick each soft needle head with a reed dipped in oil or by using the long tongs or with an optical glass pipette.
And the pimples should be pricked in their first eruption using this method; it does not increase or dissipate its effectiveness and frees him of his suffering except after exhausting the pus through scratching.
The sixty-fifth chapter.
In discussing the bleeding that occurs during artery ligation.
Blood often leaks from an artery that has been cut during a wound exposed from the outside or when cutting a tumor or organ and parts, making it difficult to cut.
If this happens to someone, quickly extend your hand towards the mouth of the artery and place your index finger on it, gently pulling until blood is contained under your finger and nothing leaks out. Then, heat up several small and large oil-dipping needles in a fire until they become intensely hot.
Then, she takes one either small or large depending on the wound and where the vessel ruptured. She then applies the forceps to the same vein after removing your finger with the wheel, holding onto the forceps until the blood is cut off.
If, upon lifting your finger from the opening of the artery, and extinguishing the forceps, take another forceps with the wheel from the furnace prepared forceps. Continue this procedure with one after another until the blood is cut off.
And be cautious not to burn a nerve if there is one, for this may cause blindness. Understand that when blood flows from the artery, it cannot be permanently cut; especially if the artery is large, unless by four methods: either with force as we said or by amputation if it has not already been done. And when amputated, its ends contract and the blood stops. Alternatively, it can be tied with a tight ligature or medication that reduces blood flow may be applied to stop the bleeding with firm compression.
As for those who attempt to cut it with a ligature or by squeezing the wound, or applying burned objects and such methods; they cannot permanently stop the bleeding. If you happen to expose yourself to any of these situations without having medical assistance or medicine, it would be wise to place the affected finger directly over the wound opening, as we have described.
He should be held tightly until the blood is squeezed out and appears above the wound, on the artery and finger. It should not be rinsed with extremely cold water even after it has frozen and stopped bleeding. During this time, you need to look for a forceps or medicine as needed.
The Second Gate.
In the sections of the cut, puncture, fracture and surgical procedures and similar matters.
He said, Khalifah, we have mentioned in the first chapter all diseases that can be treated by fire and burning medicine, and its reasons and causes, as well as its tools and images of similar cases. He divided this into chapters from the beginning to ancient times.
And in this chapter, I follow that path exactly, making it easier for the student to achieve what is required...
Before I begin this, you boys should know that in this chapter there are more tricks than in the first chapter concerning fire.
And because of that, the caution should be stronger in this chapter, as much work in this field often leads to blood loss which sustains life when a wound opens or a cut is made on a tumor or discharge from pus or surgery, or removal of an arrow or cutting through a stone, and so forth, all of which are accompanied by fears and risks, resulting in death in most cases.
And I advise you to avoid falling into what might cause suspicion on you, for in this profession there are many people suffering from various illnesses; some of them have been crippled by their illness and despised death.
Due to the intensity of their suffering and length of their ailments, along with the certainty from illness that points towards death; among them are those who expend their wealth for you in hopes of your health, but their disease is deadly. Therefore, it should not be for you to assist anyone of this nature impulsively.
May your caution be stronger than your desire and concern. Do not engage in anything of this matter except after acquiring certain knowledge that is confirmed by you regarding the desired outcome. Use in all treatments for your illnesses, advancement of knowledge and warning about what leads to safety.
If there is a way for you to benefit in gaining praise, glory, mention and commendation, Allah has inspired you my children. Follow His guidance; do not prohibit yourselves from correctness and success. Indeed, that is within his power. There is no god but Him.
And this chapter has been organized into sections based on what was discussed in the previous chapter from the hourglass to the sand clock, so that it may relieve you of any need for what you want if God willing.
The first chapter.
In the treatment of water that collects at the head of infants.
This condition, lithiasis, often affects infants at birth if the mother presses the head of the baby roughly during delivery. It may also occur for an unknown reason that is not identified.
I have not seen this cause in anyone other than infants, and every one of them that I saw from among them died quickly. That's why I avoided working on it. And I have seen an infant whose head was completely filled with water, the head increased every day. Until he could no longer sit on himself due to the enormity of his head and the humidity increased until it killed him.
This humidity either gathers between the skin and bone or under the bone on the skull. In this case, if the humidity is present in the space between the skin and bone and the tumor is small, it should be incised with a single longitudinal cut through the head until the water flows out; this is what we call the surgeon's technique.
If the humidity is greater and the tumor is larger, make it two intersecting cuts like this:.
And if the humidity is under the bone, its sign is to see that the head's seams are open from every side and water will decrease when you squeeze it with your hand inside; this should not be hidden from you. It would be appropriate to make three cuts in the middle of the head like this:.
After the incision, all moisture is drained out then the incisions are tightened by sutures and dressings. Then they are irrigated with water and oil up to the fifth day. Afterwards, the bandage is removed and the wound is treated with ointments and poultices without over-tightening the head scarves or feeding the patient on anything that's wet or highly moisturizing.
Until the member strengthens and recovers, another aspect of this involves observing where the bone of the tumor appears and the location where water (or possibly, fluid) collects. This is because it might be in the back of the head, or at the front, or on the right side, or in the north direction.
You are referring to making the incision where you see the tumor and the accumulation of water; so, you make the cut as much as possible, while being careful not to sever a vessel causing excessive bleeding that may lead to death from blood loss along with draining out moisture.
The Second Chapter.
Cutting the two arteries behind the ears, known as the hissiyis.
If someone experiences severe attacks affecting the eyes or chest, and medications have failed to alleviate this despite long duration, inform them of performing surgery on these two arteries.
If you wish to cut them, you should shave the patient's head with a scythe. Then carve the area roughly until the artery appears. Next, fasten the neck of the patient with a woollen garment. After that, locate where the pulse beats and their positions which are behind the ears in two places. Not all people hide anything else except for some individuals.

Blood sends six streams into the interposition, and perhaps it sends more or less; all of this depends on what you perceive in terms of the strength of the patient's blood flow and the saturation of his arteries. Then look at the wound; if there is something left from the scrotum after reaching the bone, cut it.
To avoid exposing an inflamed tumor, then suture the wound with a thread from a silk fabric. Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
The third chapter.
Suturing the veins in the axilla.
If a person experiences chronic constipation or severe, acute episodes due to hot and dry conditions and heat in the axillary muscles, or chronic intense headache and similar issues, and treated with various medical treatments without success. This would help to get rid of any clots from every direction. If the artery is thin, you would wrap its tip in the cannula. Then, cut off from it a part that extends its ends and you would tighten it without causing bleeding. If it doesn't heal or doesn't get detached, then blood won't flow at all. Then, drain the blood through six to three outlets.
If the artery is large, it should be tied in two places with a strong double thread. Let the thread either be from wool or from the strings of the guitar so that before the wound heals and becomes joined, mold does not rush to spread and cause bleeding.
Then cut a part between the ligatures. You do this at that moment or after some other time, and if you wish to harden it by striking bones with an iron scalpel until its tips get detached. This action is repeated or improved as we said.
Unless there is fever or mood swings in the patient, because hardening aids in eliminating fluids and makes it more effective. If during your work there is bleeding from the artery, act immediately either by hardening or by filling the area with lead and tightening your hand until the blood stops. If nothing stops it, place your finger to congeal the blood.
And conclude the position with intense cold water until the pain subsides and you adhere to what should be done, and it is easier than cutting the vein by pressing this two-edged tool on the sweat after learning the positions with the needle.
And let the midwife press it very deeply until it reaches the bone, causing sweating in two places to make the sweat spread between its sides. This is because it does not heal like this at all; here is a picture of this tool.
The edges of the two blades resemble small knuckles, but they are much sharper than many knives because if they were as sharp as a knife, cold would have reached them faster and the flesh would not have been cut quickly. If there is some roughness in both, fire will stick to both.
The flesh is cut quickly, and this operation is better than any other work and it is easier and lighter. Let there be the thickness of a finger between the two blades.

In treating the constant hot bleeding to the eyes.

It happens deep in the head with severe, painful headache and continuous sneezing. If you notice these symptoms, know that such discharges come from many deep sweat glands. The Sixth Chapter.
In the treatment of what falls into the ear.
All that falls into the ear is of four kinds, either a metallic ore-like stone or something similar to it like iron and glass, or a plant-based seed like chickpeas and kernels, and so on, or a liquid thing such as water and vinegar, etc.
If it is an animal, if a stone or a type of stone that does not exceed the ear falls in the ear, receive sunlight with the ear. If you see something greasy from buttercup or scissors stuck in it then try to remove it by movement of the head or shaking with forceps. Close the snuffers when coughing comes after placing a loop of wire or wool around the ear, and extend the ear upwards. It often comes out with this treatment; if it doesn't come out, try removing it with gentle tweezers as shown in these images.
If it comes out with the tweezers, otherwise try to remove it with a dim lighted candle with little bend. If it doesn't come out even then, make a copper tube and insert one end of the tube smoothly into the ear hole.
Fill what surrounds the tube with greased wax to prevent any other path for wind, then pull it with your breath strongly and frequently. It often comes out this way; if it doesn't come out as described or even so, take a small piece from bird molasses or the manipulated wax used for catching birds, put it in one end of the syringe.
After tightly wrapping it with a piece of string, then gently insert it into the ear hole after drying the ear from moisture. If it doesn't come out through all we described, start cutting before a boil occurs or a seizure happens.
The method of cutting is to cut the wax in the candle first, then let out a bit of blood according to its strength. Then hold the wax between your hands and turn it upwards. Cut a small incision at the base of the ear where its fat exists at its lower position.
The cut will be crescent-shaped until it reaches the stone, then remove it with what you can of the machines. Then stitch the cut as quickly as you can and treat it until it heals.
And if the thing that has fallen into one of the ear from one of the grains that grow and fatten, try to remove it with what we have mentioned. If this does not work for removal, take a soft thin forceps in accordance with this description.
Try to cut that type of grain that has fallen into the ear with it, and do this only if you are sure that that grain has become fragmented by the steam in the ear until it turns into many small pieces, then remove it using a blind sinner or a gentle hook or with tweezers.
As we mentioned, it facilitates its removal, and as for the water entering the ear, it should be used first with a camel's urine gargle. It fills his ear with some used cotton which is lying on that wet ear, and if it was removed by this method.
And if not, take many pebbles along the fingers that are smooth and grind them a little with fire. And insert one of its urine pellets into her ear hole and blow on one of her legs from this side, and strike another stone on the stone in the ear.
He continues doing this with a stone after another until all the water is removed, and he removes the water by taking one of the camel's wool or feather, inserting its single end into the ear, heating the other end till it burns most of it, then repeats the feather.
Repeat this several times until all the water is removed or draws it by the tube as previously described with the stone. As for removing the animal inside, look if it is small in body like the grasshopper and similar, then treat it with what we have mentioned in the section and otherwise.
If the size of the object is large and it is visible to touch, attempt to remove it using tweezers and forceps; this will make removal easier than any other method used in ear problems. As for removing wax that has hardened in the ear, if you have treated it as described in our section on warts and didn't succeed with your treatment.
You should look at the ear in sunlight. If you see something of wax, remove it with tweezers or delicate forceps. If you do not see anything from them, take this tube to photograph it.
Make it narrow at the bottom and wide at the top, then insert the delicate tip of this tool into the ear as far as the patient can bear. Then firmly push it in several times until all wax is removed. If it does not come out, seal around the tube with beeswax as we taught you for stones.
If it does not come out as we have instructed, use the methods mentioned earlier which were first tried to kill wax and you will find this in the section on warts. Your application of oils and medicines inside the ear would be done with this tool, here is its depiction:
As you see, it is made of silver or brass. It's narrow at the bottom with a small hole and wide on top. You can make sure that the gun inside the tube is solid if you want, or you could leave it hollow. If desired, take a piece of cotton and tightly wrap it around the end of the tube.
Then place the oil, juice or any of these medicines in the tube. It is inside the ear. Place the cotton wad at the top and squeeze it moderately with your hand until the oil flows into the auditory canal and you feel its effect.
Insert inside the wound, and let whatever you insert into the ear have been slightly heated by fire. Be careful not to allow it to be too cold or excessively hot for the ear cannot bear this.
The Seventh Chapter.
In the treatment of obstruction in the ear.
Some children may be born without having been cut, both from their mothers' wombs and in their ears.
It may also expose some people to obstruction in the ear canal due to a wound or a graft there, and this obstruction can be at the depth of an eardrum that cannot be seen by the eye.
It may extend slightly outside the hole and be visible. And you inspect it, if I see the obstruction visibly, open it with a gentle pair of forceps; this is its appearance:".
It will have a slight protrusion at one end, limited by itself and the other sides of the forceps; these are smooth to avoid injuring the ear. If the obstruction is due to growth of flesh in the ear canal, hold it with a soft hook and cut it very gently until all flesh is removed.
If the obstruction is deep in the ear, take a gentle smooth probe and slightly heat it in fire. Then place this inside the ear canal. If you feel the obstruction along with what the doctor feels of heaviness of hearing, gently remove it.
Be cautious not to damage the nerve of the ear and then insert a wick in the ear as long as the size of the hole, which has been soaked in Egyptian ointment. Do this for days until it heals without scarring or else take out the wick dipped in water with some powdered sulfur.

Chapter Eight.
In the treatment of boils that appear on the cheeks.
These boils that appear on the eyelids, they can be moist or dry. It is necessary to hold them with a comb or a pincushion and cut them from their roots with scissors then apply it with powder in the affected area.

In the treatment of colds affecting the cheeks of the eye.

The tenth chapter.
In treating the condition that appears in the eyelid.
The condition known as 'sharqan' refers to a formation of skin that occurs in the layers of the upper eyelid. This is more common among boys, causing heaviness on their eyes and making them prone to night attacks due to exposure. They are unable to look directly into sunlight. Because tears speed towards them.
Thus, you see them leaning on their faces always, sleeping with it, and their eyelids are damp due to the puffiness of the condition known as 'nto' which is noticeable externally. When you press that area with your fingers, you can feel the 'nto'. The purpose of this treatment is to have him place his head in a hole (in the wall or ground), called 'the hole', so that he might be cured.
Then take a thread of cotton, prepare a wick from it and make a circle with the wick around the 'nto' (the condition) on every side. Place this around the affected area and apply pressure from each side using your fingers to gather the 'nto' in the middle of the circle.
Then cut a groove in the middle of this moisture using the sharp tool 'nashl' across, without letting the cut be larger than the cut that would occur naturally at the edge. In depth, it should be necessary to cut through all the skin down to the 'nto'.
In most cases, the eyelid protrudes from the cut in the form of a piece of white fat which you draw out with a probe that you have wrapped between your fingers to the outside while moving your hand back and forth. Be careful not to deepen the cut for fear of injuring the eye by letting the gouging tool reach it.
If the eyelid doesn't appear at the first cut, it may be necessary to increase the depth of the cut slightly and gently until the eyelid appears. Then you should draw it out as we have explained before. You should then soak a probe in a solution of vinegar and water and place it on the area, tightening it with a bandage. Some people use salt for pressing instead.
He should place it in the cavity of the cut to dissolve what is left of that moisture. Then, he should treat it until it heals. If there was heat and an inflamed area occurred at the site, it should be treated with soothing ointments until it heals.
The eleventh chapter.
In the methods of eye watering.
If a new eyelash grows above the natural path under the normal eyelashes, it can harm the eye and cause various diseases such as constant watering of the eyes, drooping eyelids, whitening, and swelling. This can even be a reason for the failure of the eyesight itself if not treated properly.
Eye watering can be done in four ways: either by rubbing with fire as described under the section of rubbing, or by using a strong medicine as previously mentioned. Alternatively, it could involve cutting and sewing, or dabbing as I have mentioned.
You should make the eyelid head towards your finger, then flip the eyelid with your left hand. If it flips properly, otherwise insert a needle in the lower part of the eyelash and drive the needle through from above using the thread. This makes sure the thread is close to the hair itself, pulling the thread up by the eyelash.
Turn it with the forceps, then cut in the inner eyelid without cutting excess hair from the lower eyelid, starting from the larger maeck (eyelid) to the smaller one. Then remove the thread and place a small pad of cotton or lace under the eyelid, finally sew on the eyelid with silk.
Like the shape of an Ace card, but it should be according to how much you want to lift your eyelid as this varies among people; some may need to cut from their eyelid enough that suits when their eyelids are relaxed.
And some may need to cut less of this, according to how relaxed their eyelids are. Then you use the forceps along the two lines that you have taught, starting from the larger maeck (eyelid) to the smaller one. The incision is made close to the natural hairline with a firmness akin to pressing with your finger nails.
Then, the needle enters one of the corners of the skin, then removes it completely. The lips are sewn together using a needle and a fine thread of silk or wool. The blood is wiped away, and what remains of the threads is attached to some hanging things if necessary.
You may do it as you wish, or it doesn't matter either way. The stitches and threads will stay for about three to four days, then treat the wound accordingly. You could leave the cut open without stitches and treat it with something that dries and constricts, because when the wound heals and the edges come together, lifting of the eyelid occurs. Stitches are better in this regard.
This aspect of the incision, I mentioned at the beginning except that it has a drawback on the blind, which is effective and without danger. Another aspect in the incision is that you should make an incision on the eyelid like the shape of an Ace card as described. Then lift the eyelid with three needles that are either separated or grouped as in this picture.
Then cut the excess eyelid with small scissors as shown in this image, cutting appropriately.

Then, bring another thread close to the larger loop and a third thread close to the smaller one. Gather the threads between your fingers with moderation, then lift them up in a moderate manner.
And lift the taught skin as described. Then stitch both lips of the wound together with sewing, and treat it until it heals. If there is a hot tumor upon cutting or splitting, use the cimicifuga (a type of plant) and similar soothing ointments to alleviate it.
The lower eyelid may also cause its lashes to turn inward. It is necessary to use the methods of cutting, sewing, and cauterization mentioned earlier, as well as applying medicine or cauterizing with fire for it. Applying medicine or cauterizing with fire will either be more intense or gentler on the patient than cutting and sewing, depending on the specific situation.
Caulking with a tube is done in this manner; you turn the lid over and cut along the inner slit as described. Then, make two or three sticks about half an inch long, parallel to the length of the eyelid and narrower than its width.
I have borrowed from each end on both sides, where the threads grab hold. Then gather them gently with what is preferable of the eyelid. Pull the sticks together firmly from each side. Leave it for some days as the tightened skin dies, turns black and decays.
Until she spontaneously stops, if her bleeding slows down, borrow her the amount of a loan and then treat her until she is healed. The second chapter.
In lifting the falling eyelashes through needle.
If a hair or two is causing trouble, what you should do is take a fine needle and insert there a thread of fine, smooth silk. Then gather its ends and make them a very light knot, the length of the thread being about a yard.
Then, on the smaller sticks, insert another fine thread shorter than it. If you wish, tie its ends together, then have the patient lie down with his head near your lap and close to the sun for better visibility of the work, which is precise. Then, pass the needle through the root of the excess hair with the smaller sticks.
And execute it on the eyelid with the wheel until it comes out from above the natural hair. Then draw the thread above the smaller sticks and insert the hair, whether one, two, or three, no more than that, into those sticks.
Then pull your hand with it until the hair comes out along with the sticks in the eyelid together with the natural hair. If you pulled the sticks but the hair didn't come out with them, you've pulled the sticks down with the thread that was inserted into them until they come out of the upper hole.
Then insert the hair again and pull them. Do this until it rises in the upper hole and you can see it, then release the sticks and thread and remove them. Tighten your eye for two or three days till it secures the hair in place and flesh grows on it.
If the thread is short, either you add to it a long hair from your natural hair which will grow with it, or you leave it until it grows longer, then when that happens you cut it.
The thirteenth chapter.
In the treatment of trichiasis that occurs in the upper eyelid.
The one affected by this trichiasis is called an arnautical. This trichiasis can be either natural or accidental. The accidental kind arises from a surgical incision, a cut, or tearing and so forth.
The purpose of the operation is to cut through this adhesion and separate its edges, leaving a thread-like opening between them. It should be held in place until it heals. There should not be used for treating such issues things that dry out or constrict.
If you do that, the trichiasis will return worse than before. Instead, use things that relax such as the hoop and the tenter with water that has been infused with a little myrrh, cotton juice, Diakhil's ointment dissolved with some fat, and grease it with it and treat it accordingly.
The solution to treating it is to try every possible way not to return to its initial condition. The operation we mentioned is some kind of repair for the trichiasis, rather than restoring the place's shape according to how it was originally.
The fourteenth chapter.
In the treatment of trichiasis that occurs in the lower eyelid.
This trichiasis that occurs at the bottom is actually called trichiasis. It can be either natural or accidental. The accidental kind arises from a surgical incision, cut, or tear and so forth.
The method is to take a needle with two threads and pierce it in the flesh, then penetrate it from the left margin of the wound to the right margin until the thread becomes inside both sides of the flesh. Then elevate the flesh by the needle and cut it with a broad scissor.
If the eyelid returns to its original shape as it should, otherwise you take a thread and place it at the site of the cut. Then you turn the eyelid with it, making two cuts inside the eyelid's edge. The ends of these cuts are from the corners of the cut area until they meet; forming an angle. Even if they join, its shape becomes similar to this form:.
And it is the Greek letter lambda, then you remove that flesh as much as its sharp side is below what follows the eyelid. Then you join the separated parts with two threads and sew them with wool thread. Then treat it with the medications we mentioned before the relaxing and bleeding ones until it heals.
If the incision, stitch, or line was exposed, then it should be cut with a simple incision without removing any hair. Then separate between the lips by bleeding as mentioned before.
And the saying in treating a horizontal or vertical incision is to perform the operation according to how you determine from the shape of the incision, for it can have many variations in appearance. The surgeon devises the trick with whatever means he can manage.
Until the appearance returns to its natural state or gets close to it, and the disease itself guides you as to what is suitable for work and machinery in most cases.

Chapter Forty.
He makes use of speech in removing tumors and cutting them.
Tumors come in many varieties, each differentiated according to what is detailed one by one in this book. They vary in their treatment and incision based on two aspects: the first being the nature of the tumor itself and what it contains from moisture.
The second type of lesion is determined by the location in the body since a tumor occurring in the head differs from one that occurs in the buttocks, and a tumor occurring in a fever-prone area differs from one occurring in a joint. Each one has its own rule for treatment.
Among tumors, there are those that should not be drained until the pus matures and is complete, and among them, there are some that can be drained even if the maturation of the pus has not reached completion. This refers to tumors that occur near joints.
Because if a tumor occurs near a joint and extends until it starts to rot around it, it might spoil the ligaments or nerves of that joint. This can become a cause for the stagnation of that member or the tumor is close to a main body part.
Because if you delay the drainage until it matures, you might damage that main body part or it may occur near the buttocks. In this case, you should drain it intentionally. But, what is necessary to drain is not fully matured in tumors close to the buttocks to avoid rotting and entering inside the buttocks, which could become an invader.
There is also a certain point where they do not heal completely, and you should learn the time to drain tumors that have fully matured. This occurs when there is no pain in the tumor, the fever has subsided, the redness has decreased, and when there is pulsation under the skin and other signs are present.
It is necessary to place the drain at the bottom of the tumor's location if possible, for easier drainage downwards or towards the deeper part of the tumor and with more precision. Let the drain be horizontal if the tumors are located near the limbs.
In the locations of muscles, tendons, nerves and veins as well as generally in all flat areas without curvature, but if there is a curvature then it should be cut according to that location. As for tumors in muscular areas, it's better to leave the cutting until later.
Until it hardens as we said until the completion, if you cut it before that, its drainage would be prolonged and abundant, it might become very impure. There could also be a risk of stiffening its lips and its cavity. Some tumors may need to be cut on the width of the body when necessary or according to what the organ needs.
It is advisable to use a single cut for small tumors and a wide or many incisions for large ones, according to the size of the tumor. Some tumors may require skin grafting and cutting if they have become like a scratch.
There are cases where it has become like what is observed in many abscesses and hiding places, from which it may split into three angles, and there are cases where it is cut like the shape of an ace card as in the case of the aortic tumor.
Some cases require the use of a circular cut, a crescent-shaped cut and similar incisions, where there is no protruding head like in flat tumors that are not raised. It's best to make a simple single cut for such cases. And when it comes to large tumors that have been treated over a long period, if you were to remove them all at once, it might lead to the sudden release of pus.
Instead, remove some of it first, then pull the tumor on another day and also remove some pus as well. Do this in stages repeatedly until all of it is removed.
Especially if the patient is weak or a pregnant woman, a child, an elderly person, or someone with a chronic illness; the animal spirit often dissipates along with the pus release. It might be that the patient dies without you noticing, so beware of this aspect very seriously.

Chapter Fifty-One
In Chapter fifty-one, dealing with hemorrhoids that bleed and their removal, as well as treatment for fissures.
The hemorrhoids can be divided into two, either they are inside the anus resembling the veins of a horse's hoof or like raisins from grapes, being small and large. Blood constantly leaks from them.
They can occur singly or in abundance, both inside and outside the anus. However, those occurring externally are less common and tend to have little moisture, leaking yellow water or slightly bloody fluids continuously, with a body-like color.
For the hemorrhoids inside the anus, you should instruct the patient to evacuate their bowels and cleanse themselves until they can see the stool coming out, so that you can observe the hemorrhoids. Then treat it with all other remedies until you see improvement. For those stools that come out from outside the anus, these are simpler cases to manage.
This involves gripping them with your finger or attaching them to a string and cutting them, then treating them with what we've discussed until they heal. If you dislike cutting using iron tools, it might be better to use this method of herbarium; take a twisted thread and insert an awl into it.
Then draw the worms upwards and extract them with a needle from its original place from the other side. She does this to all the worms leaving one that she does not pinch.
To remove the blood clots from it, then she places on the stool an incision dipped in oil, resin or tallow and puts it on the stool. She commands the patient to remain still and leaves him until he urinates. When the urine is complete, she treats the wounds with ointments and other treatments until she heals.
As for the treatment of fissures, it often appears due to dryness from fecal matter and trapping of the skin. If there are no complications and it has not healed in him, then medication might be necessary, so it should be treated with the scalpel or your finger until it becomes moist and the upper layer of skin that prevents its healing is removed.
Then treat it until it heals as necessary, if it does not heal, repeat the process with more rigor than before until it fully heals and sheds properly. Then treat it again; he will recover.

The 44th chapter.
In the treatment of wounds.
I have mentioned in the division about treating things similar to cauterization, and here I am mentioning their treatment by hand and with medications at perfection. I say that injuries vary according to what is present during surgery and according to where the injury occurs.
The things that are present during surgeries are numerous, like a rock fracture or cut from a sword or knife, or a spear thrust or arrow and such a variety of other things.
And as for injuries according to body positions, like the injury that occurs on the head or neck or chest or abdomen or liver and such organs.

I say that if a simple head injury occurred, and there was no bone fracture, I looked at it. Chapter Fifty-Eight.
In the surgery of the abdomen and removal of entrails, and suturing.
A perforation of the abdomen can be large, small or medium. The larger one may expel intestines or several parts of it, making its insertion and suturing more difficult.
A small perforation can also be more difficult for another reason - it requires that returning the organs is even harder. If the intestines do not quickly return to their place, they swell and become hard, making their insertion more difficult. This is why a moderate-sized perforation has proven better than these two types, as it does not make it as difficult to return the intestines compared to them.
Know that sewing the abdomen is on four aspects. The two stitches mentioned are capable of being used in sewing the abdomen and all other body surgeries. The remaining two stitches are general for all surgeries except they are specialized particularly for sewing the abdomen.
And I will describe to you one, explained and detailed. If the wound is small and something of the intestine has come out from it and returning it was difficult, this could be for two reasons: either due to the smallness of the tear as we said, or because the air's cold caused swelling in its passage.
If this is the case, it would be necessary to warm it by immersing a sponge or cloth in hot water only, or perhaps after cooking it with garlic and onions. The intestine should be rubbed until the swelling dissolves.
And it may do that drinking the drink with thickened extract which is better than water alone in dissolving swelling. If you see the swelling dissolved, wet the intestines in cooked soup or baker's broth; he will flow into its place more easily because of this lubrication.

The seventy-eighth chapter.
In amputations and dispersing of bones.
The limbs may decay for a reason from outside or inside. If that corruption is treated with medicinal treatments and the treatment fails, and you see the corruption advancing in the member without anything deterring it.

Chapter Eighty-One.
In the treatment of abscesses and methods of administering medicines to them.
If a tumor occurs in some of the fleshly organs and prolongs for a period until it has been present for as long as its duration, then it might burst or rupture and all that was inside it from the length of time would come out, leaving the place empty as if it were a vessel.

The ninety-ninth chapter.
In cutting ligaments.

Chapter fifty-nine.
In opening the civilian's sweat gland.

In the cut made on the worm that develops under the gallbladder, it is called the cow's cause.
This disease is called "the cow's cause" in some of our countries because it occurs frequently in cows, and it is a small worm that develops between the skin and muscle. It moves throughout the body upwards and downwards.

Chapter Three and Ninety.
In cutting through the disease known as nafar.
This disease, which in our country is called nafar, is a pain that manifests in some organs and then moves from one organ to another. I have seen it as described for you.
I was summoned to treat an invalid woman in some oases. I uncovered her arm and detected a slight puffing under the sweat of the arm's artery. When an hour had passed, I saw that puff continuing with the bandage as if it were an infection ascending to the elbow like a worm at its fastest speed imaginable, as fast as lead.
If the pain shifted from one place to another, it would disappear from that spot and settle in the thigh. Then, after an hour had passed, it spread throughout her body until it reached the other arm. She then told me that her entire body was rotating as I observed.
I was astonished by the speed at which it moved from one limb to another, and I had not seen this disease with such characteristics before. However, I have observed groups who found that pain would move from one limb to another, but I saw it in this manner for the first time in this woman.
I did not realize this until I understood that the woman was from Bedouin people who are generally naked and have exposed skin. It's due to this that the moving wind could be felt, and it would not occur in those with well-kept bodies and hidden skin.
And if you want to treat him and he feels pain, it will become evident to you as we have described. Tighten above and below him with the wheel and cut him until that trapped wind comes out and cleans the area.
If you do not see it with your own eyes, treat him by purging the body and what drives winds away like the seeds of garlic and the seeds of saffron, among other medicines.
The fourth and ninety-first chapter.
In the removal of arrows.
Arrows can vary depending on their types and the parts of the body where they are located. As for the variation according to their types, some are large and small, while others are made of glass (either hollow or solid), and there are those with three angles and four angles.
Some of them have tongues and others have fragments. As for those that fit with the organs they occur in, they are divided into two types: either the organs are among primary hollow ones such as brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, stomach, bladder, etc., or they are not. If an arrow falls into one of these organs and shows symptoms of death that I will describe to you later, it is necessary to avoid removing that arrow from it; for death usually overtakes its owner. If these bad signs do not appear and the arrow is not hidden in the depth of the organ, remove it and treat the wound. As for symptoms related to the brain when hit by an arrow that pierces through bone and wounds the area above the brain, one is exposed to severe headache, fever, and dizziness.
If these bad signs do not appear and the arrow is not hidden in the depth of the organ, remove it and treat the wound. As for symptoms related to the brain when hit by an arrow that pierces through bone and wounds the area above the brain, one is exposed to severe headache, fever, and dizziness. Eye and tongue inflammation, muscle twitching, confusion, fits, and possibly bleeding from the nostrils or ears. Speech may be lost with no sound, and white moisture similar to dough appears at the wound site that leaks out like meat juice.
If these symptoms appear, refrain from treating the wounded individual or removing the arrow if it hasn't already been removed. As for arrow symptoms when it hits the heart and is close to the left chest; you feel as if it has pierced something solid rather than an empty space.
Perhaps the arrow exhibits a movement resembling heartbeats, and blood of a dark color flows from the wound. Followed by the limbs turning cold, a chill sweat, and fainting; know that death is imminent. As for an arrow piercing the lung symptom, bleeding of fatty matter follows from the wound.
The veins around the neck swell, and the patient's urine changes color. They breathe with a loud noise and request cold air to inhale. If the arrow hits the lung shield in the chest, it is usually close to the smaller ribs, causing heavy breathing along with intense pain.
And the organs of the abdomen convulse and move, if the arrow hits the liver it follows this with severe pain and blood comes out of the wound resembling liver in its color. If the arrow hits the stomach then perhaps food emerges from the wound that is not compacted.
His condition is evident. If the arrow hits the abdomen and causes bleeding or pus to come out of the wound or incision, there is no hope for his treatment nor for extracting the arrow. If the arrow hit the bladder and urine came out, then that indicates a different course of action needs to be taken.
Something protruded from it, and the pain intensified for the sick man. Know that he is dead. As for other organs such as the face, eyes, neck, shoulder, back, muscles of the back, quadriceps, legs and similar body parts have accepted the most probable situation.
If the arrow did not hit a vessel or nerve, and if the arrow was not poisoned, I will inform you about some things that I have seen regarding these arrows to guide your treatment. That being said, an arrow struck a man in the root of his eye socket.
I removed it for him from the other side under his earlobe, he was cleansed and no harm occurred to his eye. I also removed another arrow which had hit a Jew in the inner part of his eyelid below his lower lid. The arrow had vanished inside but only its small tip stuck out, attached to the wood.

He did not experience any bad event afterwards. I saw a man who had an arrow hit him on his back; the wound adhered to him.
And after seven years had passed, the arrow came out from his thigh root. I saw a woman who had an arrow hit her in her abdomen; the wound adhered to her and remained there, without any change in her condition or did she find it causing harm at anything of her natural actions.
I saw another man who had an arrow hit him in his face; the wound adhered to him and he didn't find much pain from it, there are many like this. I also removed an arrow from one of the Sultan's commanders, who had been hit in the middle of his nose slightly tilted towards the right side.

Chapter Two.
In the open fracture on the head.
The types of open fractures on the head are numerous, their shapes vary, and their causes are diverse. Some fractures occur due to a sword strike, which may either completely heal the bone until it reaches the sinus beneath the bone. Similarly, it can be done with wood as well.
Therefore, this type of fracture is called comminuted and may also occur when the sword cuts through part of the bone but does not pierce its entire length. This type of fracture is called a segmental break and can result in either large or small wounds.
This excerpt discusses "fractures that are brittle or compressed, whose cause might be a blow with a stone or falling onto a rock or something similar. This kind of fracture can either puncture the membrane underneath the bone, or it can occur in the face of the bone.
This excerpt continues by stating that the wounds from these fractures can either be large or small, and there are also fractures which remain hidden within the bone in its hair-like structure; they are gradual breaks.
This type of fracture is thus called 'hair-like' or 'hairline', and there are fractures caused by a fall or hitting with a stone, among others that enter the sheet of bone into its interior turning the location into a bending point. Depending on where it gets struck, part of this can enter inside.
This type of fracture is most often found in the soft bone of the head, like children's skull bones. All these types of fractures can have clean or unclean fragments. We will address how to treat all this at their respective places and we will identify each type of fracture by examining them.
This involves examining it with probes, removing the rotten flesh from its surface. For hair-like fractures, you can identify them by inspecting the bone and rubbing with ink; if the fracture appears black. As for treating a fracture, one should first look at the symptoms of disease.

Death is often inevitable with these symptoms in most cases.
And if I see symptoms that are not alarming and I hope for his safety, then you should proceed with his treatment. For instance, if the wounded person was injured at the very beginning of being wounded, and it happened in winter's days.
In any case, one should strive to remove the bone before the fourteenth day. If it is within summer days, it would be advisable to hasten removal of the bone before the seventh day in order to prevent corruption under the bone from the lining, thus exposing those symptoms which we have described.

The Third Chapter.
To set the nose if it breaks.
Know that the nasal bone can only break either its upper fissure completely or one of them, as they are bones. The lower part is made of cartilage and does not break, but it is subjected to swelling, bruising, and inflammation.
If one of its fissures breaks, you should insert the small finger into the hole in the nose and smooth out that break from inside with your ring finger and thumb on the outside until the nose returns to its natural shape. Do this gently, and be sure not to cause any pain or injury to the patient.
If the break is at the top of the nose and the finger cannot reach it, you should smooth out that break using a slightly rough end on the inside. If the break occurs in both sides, do the same, and start setting it on the first day after the break occurred.
If possible, then after the seventh or tenth day when the hot swelling subsides, you should insert a thread of silk into the hole in the nose if the break is on one side, or two threads if the break affects both sides.
Make the thread rough enough to fill the hole in the nose. Some of those who set the bone advised at first to grease the thread with tallow and change it every day, but I do not agree with that; instead, you should grease the thread with the white part of an egg mixed with camel's urine.
Then the child is left to grow until the bone sets and cartilage hardens. In some cases, when in place of the incision made during delivery, feather tubes from an owl are inserted into the nose after wrapping them with a soft cut, making it more difficult for the nose to break and preventing the obstruction from interfering with breathing.
And this is not necessary if you choose to create them, or if you choose to create small mustaches. If the nose presents during your work and there's a hot burn, you can moisten the nose with cork or cotton dipped in honey and oil, or something from the deaxilons' ointment.

The ninth section.

The eleventh chapter.
In levering the fracture of the humerus.
The humerus is between the shoulder blade and the shoulder joint. If it fractures, lever it on two sides. One of these is to take a flexible, smooth, thickened reed in this form:
And tie it at its ends with two straps. Then hang it from a high place, having the sick person sit on a chair. Then lay his broken arm over the reed so that his elbow sticks in the middle of the bend of the reed. Then hang something heavy above him.
Or have a servant extend it downwards, then the doctor will correct the fracture with both hands until the break returns to where it should. The other way is for the sick person to lie on his head and hang his hand from around his neck with a strap.
Then you command servants to adjust one of them above the fracture with his hands, and the other below it, extending each one towards their sides. If you want more strength in the extension, tie a strap under the fracture and another above it, making each servant extend according to his side.
If the fracture is close to one side of the thigh, the strap should be below the elbow and the other under the fracture towards the buttock. Similarly, if the fracture is close to the buttock, the straps should be in that position and on the buttock itself.

The Fourteenth Chapter.

The sixteenth chapter.

The Nineteenth Chapter.

Chapter Nineteen.
In treating the complication that appears after some fractures.
Complications often occur following fractures, especially near joints, where the shape of the limb might be altered and it could prevent natural function.
If you notice that the complication is soft, use medications that have a constricting effect such as saffron, milk, vinegar, honey, and similar substances. Take some of these individually or in full amounts, mix them with a drink that has a constricting effect or the white part of an egg, or with lemon juice.
Carry it out on the complication with effort, pull it tightly for a while, and leave the pulling without stopping for many days. Then stop the pulling and start again until the complication leaves, God willing, or secure a sheet of well-polished lead over it.
Lead has the property of removing all that is stuck within organs. If the complication has hardened and tightened to such a degree that removal becomes necessary, cut through it from above or remove the fatty outgrowths or cut them off with some small pieces until it goes away, then treat the wound until it heals.
Chapter Twenty-One.
In treating fractures, if the patient was forcibly manipulated and afterward found soft or waxy in texture, not according to its original state.
If the bones are forcibly broken and afterward, the member remains soft and weak, there are many reasons for this. One of the reasons could be either excessive manipulation of ligaments and tying them in a way that is not appropriate, or pulling the ligaments excessively to the point where food cannot enter the body, or because of extreme beating, or excessive movements at inappropriate times, or due to lack of blood in the emaciated person's body making it weak.
To treat this condition, one should feed the emaciated person and enrich their body so that there is an abundance of blood in it. The use of baths and bringing joy and happiness to them can also be helpful. Then, hanging weights on the limb can help attract much food or keep it moist with warm water for a long time. Until food starts to go through him and return to its natural state.
Chapter Twenty-Two.
In treating broken bones, if they are forcibly bent and prevent the limb from functioning as it should.
If an organ that has been forcibly manipulated after its healing, appears twisted or bent due to the deformity of the broken bone or complications resulting in a distorted appearance of the limb. Many of our doctors and enforcers have been doing this in our country.
This action is highly condemned, leading to a great deception through the tight pinch, but if the deformity and intricacy are nature's design, it would be advisable to use water that has boiled with relaxed herbs such as mint leaves, its root, crown of the king and similar.
It is sealed with softened ingredients like the tight substance of the da'axil or a drop from the root of mint is taken and mixed with chicken fat, then applied. Or a drop from the sweet fig is soaked in it along with hen's dung, or other medicines called as those that prevent buckling.
The complexity is dissolved through constant, gentle rubbing done with hands and the movement of limbs towards all directions at all times. If deformity has occurred and worsened to become rigid, it becomes necessary to treat it with iron when such a condition arises.
It is necessary to cut through the upper part, releasing the connection of bones and cutting off what has been preferred of complexity or bone in thin segments. Effort and care must be used in this process, then treat the wound as described until it heals.
The twenty-third chapter.
The jaw is a joint that, when it moves out of its place, hinders movement and disfigures the organ, causing severe pains and discomfort to the patient. If someone presents with a jaw problem, one should promptly take action to correct it immediately.

The twenty-fourth chapter.
In the treatment of dental extraction from below.

The twenty-fifth chapter.
In returning the hip bone and the lower leg joint.

The twenty-sixth chapter.
In the treatment of relieving hip dislocation.
Know that the dislocated hip can move in three directions: one, it may move towards the knee and downwards; two, it may move towards the chest, or even upwards, which happens rarely.
It does not move backward to the place of the shoulder, nor forward to the location of the nerve. It mostly moves downwards and outwards towards the knee, especially in those with little flesh because it quickly exits and re-enters them.
As for those with ample flesh, it behaves differently; it exits and enters with difficulty. Sometimes, due to a hit or fall, the hip swells up hotly and one might mistake this for dislocation. It should be tested in such cases until its health is confirmed.
Then, when treating it, you advance in its cure. The twenty-seventh chapter.
In treating the dislocation of the shoulder.
The shoulder joint dislocates with difficulty, and it also returns with difficulty. It dislocates in all directions, especially forward or backward. The dislocation of the shoulder is not hidden from you because it occurs under your sight and touch to whatever shape it has dislocated into.
And when you compare the dislocated shoulder to its original position, this reveals it to you clearly with palpation of the joint. It cannot bend the arm nor touch itself to you due to its inability. You should hasten and return the dislocation before it is presented to you by applying a hot pack.
If it is presented to you with a hot lump, it becomes difficult to return and may not completely heal. Especially if the dislocation is towards the back, it is the worst of all types of dislocations and has the most intense pain. It often results in death along with it.
